as required. $\square $

\section{Section 3: Statement and Proof of Additional Lemmas}

\noindent \qquad In this section, we state and prove a number of additional
supporting lemmas whose results are used to prove some of the lemmas given
in section 1 of this online appendix.

\medskip

\noindent \textbf{Lemma OA-1: }Under Assumptions 5 and 6(i), the following
statements are true.

\begin{enumerate}
\item[(a)] 
\begin{equation*}
tr\left\{ D_{\widehat{\vartheta }}^{2}\right\} =O_{a.s.}\left( \frac{%
K_{2,n}^{2}}{n}\right) ,
\end{equation*}%
where $D_{\widehat{\vartheta }}=diag\left( \widehat{\vartheta }_{1},...,%
\widehat{\vartheta }_{m_{n}}\right) $.

\item[(b)] 
\begin{equation*}
\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}\left\vert \widehat{\vartheta }%
_{\left( i,t\right) }\right\vert ^{2}=O_{a.s.}\left( \frac{K_{2,n}^{2}}{n^{2}%
}\right) .
\end{equation*}
\end{enumerate}

\noindent \textbf{Proof of Lemma OA-1:}

To show part (a), note that, by the result of Lemma 1, there exists a
constant $C>0$ such that \textbf{\ }%
\begin{eqnarray*}
tr\left\{ D_{\widehat{\vartheta }}^{2}\right\} &=&\dsum\limits_{\left(
i,t\right) =1}^{m_{n}}\widehat{\vartheta }_{\left( i,t\right) }^{2} \\
&=&d_{P^{\perp }}^{\prime }\left( M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }\circ M^{\left(
Z,Q\right) }\right) ^{-1}\dsum\limits_{\left( i,t\right)
=1}^{m_{n}}e_{\left( i,t\right) }e_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime }\left(
M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }\circ M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }\right) ^{-1}d_{P^{\perp }}
\\
&=&d_{P^{\perp }}^{\prime }\left( M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }\circ M^{\left(
Z,Q\right) }\right) ^{-2}d_{P^{\perp }} \\
&\leq &\frac{1}{\left[ \lambda _{\min }\left( M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }\circ
M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }\right) \right] ^{2}}d_{P^{\perp }}^{\prime
}d_{P^{\perp }} \\
&\leq &\left( \frac{1}{C}\right) ^{2}d_{P^{\perp }}^{\prime }d_{P^{\perp }}%
\text{ \ }a.s. \\
&=&\left( \frac{1}{C}\right) ^{2}\dsum\limits_{\left( i,t\right)
=1}^{m_{n}}\left( P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( i,t\right) }^{\perp }\right)
^{2} \\
&\leq &\left( \frac{1}{C}\right) ^{2}\left( \max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right)
\leq m_{n}}P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( i,t\right) }^{\perp }\right)
\dsum\limits_{\left( i,t\right) =1}^{m_{n}}P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left(
i,t\right) }^{\perp } \\
&=&O_{a.s.}\left( \frac{K_{2,n}^{2}}{n}\right) \text{ \ (by Assumption
5(iv)).\ \ }
\end{eqnarray*}%
where $e_{\left( i,t\right) }$ denotes an $m_{n}\times 1$ elementary vector
whose $\left( i,t\right) ^{th}$ component is $1$ and all other components
are $0$.

Next, we consider part (b). Note first that, as shown in the proof of Lemma
1, under the assumptions that $\min_{1\leq i\leq n}T_{i}\geq 3$ and $%
K_{n}/n=o(1)$, the projection matrix $M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }$ is strictly
diagonally dominate $a.s.n.$, so that there exists a positive constant $%
\underline{C}$ such that%
\begin{equation*}
\min_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}\left[ M_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left(
i,t\right) }^{\left( Z,Q\right) }\left( M_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left(
i,t\right) }^{\left( Z,Q\right) }-\frac{1}{2}\right) \right] \geq \underline{%
C}>0\text{ \ }a.s.n.
\end{equation*}%
See, in particular, expression (\ref{Hadamard eigen cond}) in the proof of
Lemma 1. Under these conditions, then, application of Theorem 1 of Varah
(1975) to our problem leads to the following inequality%
\begin{equation*}
\left\Vert \left( M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }\circ M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }\right)
^{-1}\right\Vert _{\infty }\leq \left( \min_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq
m_{n}}\left[ \left( M_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( i,t\right) }^{\left(
Z,Q\right) }\right) ^{2}-\dsum\limits_{\substack{ \left( k,\upsilon \right)
=1  \\ \left( k,\upsilon \right) \neq \left( i,t\right) }}^{m_{n}}\left(
M_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( k,\upsilon \right) }^{\left( Z,Q\right)
}\right) ^{2}\right] \right) ^{-1}\text{.}
\end{equation*}%
Now, making use of this inequality, we have, almost surely for all $n$
sufficiently large,%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}\left\vert \widehat{\vartheta }%
_{\left( i,t\right) }\right\vert ^{2} \\
&=&\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}\left\vert e_{\left( i,t\right)
}^{\prime }\left( M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }\circ M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }\right)
^{-1}d_{P^{\perp }}\right\vert ^{2} \\
&\leq &\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}\left\Vert \left( M^{\left(
Z,Q\right) }\circ M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }\right) ^{-1}e_{\left( i,t\right)
}\right\Vert _{1}^{2}\left\Vert d_{P^{\perp }}\right\Vert _{\infty }^{2}%
\text{ \ (by H\"{o}lder's inequality)} \\
&=&\left( \max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}\left\Vert \left(
M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }\circ M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }\right) ^{-1}e_{\left(
i,t\right) }\right\Vert _{1}\right) ^{2}\left\Vert d_{P^{\perp }}\right\Vert
_{\infty }^{2} \\
&=&\left( \max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}\dsum\limits_{\left(
j,s\right) =1}^{m_{n}}\left\vert \left( M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }\circ
M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }\right) _{\left( j,s\right) ,\left( i,t\right)
}^{-1}\right\vert \right) ^{2}\left( \max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq
m_{n}}P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( i,t\right) }^{\perp }\right) ^{2} \\
&=&\left\Vert \left( M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }\circ M^{\left( Z,Q\right)
}\right) ^{-1}\right\Vert _{1}^{2}\left( \max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq
m_{n}}P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( i,t\right) }^{\perp }\right) ^{2} \\
&=&\left\Vert \left( M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }\circ M^{\left( Z,Q\right)
}\right) ^{-1}\right\Vert _{\infty }^{2}\left( \max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right)
\leq m_{n}}P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( i,t\right) }^{\perp }\right) ^{2}%
\text{ \ (by symmetry of }\left( M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }\circ M^{\left(
Z,Q\right) }\right) ^{-1}\text{)} \\
&\leq &\left( \min_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}\left[ \left(
M_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( i,t\right) }^{\left( Z,Q\right) }\right)
^{2}-\dsum\limits_{\substack{ \left( k,\upsilon \right) =1  \\ \left(
k,\upsilon \right) \neq \left( i,t\right) }}^{m_{n}}\left( M_{\left(
i,t\right) ,\left( k,\upsilon \right) }^{\left( Z,Q\right) }\right) ^{2}%
\right] \right) ^{-2}\left( \max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq
m_{n}}P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( i,t\right) }^{\perp }\right) ^{2}\text{ \ 
} \\
&&\text{(by Theorem 1 of Varah, 1975)} \\
&=&\left( 2\min_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}\left[ M_{\left(
i,t\right) ,\left( i,t\right) }^{\left( Z,Q\right) }\left( M_{\left(
i,t\right) ,\left( i,t\right) }^{\left( Z,Q\right) }-\frac{1}{2}\right) %
\right] \right) ^{-2}\left( \max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq
m_{n}}P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( i,t\right) }^{\perp }\right) ^{2} \\
&\leq &\left( \frac{1}{2\underline{C}}\right) ^{2}\left( \max_{1\leq \left(
i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( i,t\right) }^{\perp
}\right) ^{2}\text{ \ (by expression (\ref{Hadamard eigen cond}))} \\
&=&O_{a.s.}\left( \frac{K_{2,n}^{2}}{n^{2}}\right) \text{. }\square
\end{eqnarray*}

\medskip

\noindent \textbf{Lemma OA-2: }

Under Assumptions 1, 2, 3(iii), and 5(iii), the following statements are
true.

\begin{enumerate}
\item[(a)] 
\begin{equation*}
\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}\left( Z_{1}^{\prime
}M^{Q}Z_{1}\right) ^{-1}Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n}}%
=O_{p}\left( 1\right) ,
\end{equation*}

\item[(b)] 
\begin{equation*}
\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n}}%
=O_{p}\left( 1\right) .
\end{equation*}

\item[(c)] 
\begin{equation*}
\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n}}=O_{p}\left( 1\right) .
\end{equation*}
\end{enumerate}

\bigskip

\noindent \textbf{Proof of Lemma OA-2:}

Note first that, under Assumption 5(iii), $Z^{\prime }M^{Q}Z$ is positive
definite $a.s.n.$, which implies that $Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}$ is
positive definite and, thus, nonsingular $a.s.n.$ as well. Now, to show part
(a), note that, for any $a\in \mathbb{R}^{d}$ such that $\left\Vert
a\right\Vert _{2}=1$, we obtain, by applying Assumptions 1, 2(i), and
3(iii), 
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&E\left[ \left( \frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime
}M^{Q}Z_{1}\left( Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}\right) ^{-1}Z_{1}^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n}}\right) ^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \\
&=&\frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}\left(
Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}\right) ^{-1}Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}E\left[
\varepsilon \varepsilon ^{\prime }|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right]
M^{Q}Z_{1}\left( Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}\right) ^{-1}Z_{1}^{\prime
}M^{Q}Z_{2}\Upsilon a}{n} \\
&\leq &\left( \max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}E\left[ \varepsilon
_{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \right) \frac{a^{\prime
}\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}\left( Z_{1}^{\prime
}M^{Q}Z_{1}\right) ^{-1}Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{2}\Upsilon a}{n} \\
&\leq &\left( \max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}E\left[ \varepsilon
_{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \right) \frac{a^{\prime
}\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }Z_{2}\Upsilon a}{n} \\
&=&O_{a.s.}\left( 1\right) \text{.}
\end{eqnarray*}%
Hence, there exists a positive constant $\overline{C}<\infty $ such that for
all $n$ sufficiently large%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&E\left( \left[ \frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime
}M^{Q}Z_{1}\left( Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}\right) ^{-1}Z_{1}^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n}}\right] ^{2}\right) \\
&=&E_{Z}\left\{ E\left( \left[ \frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime
}Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}\left( Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}\right)
^{-1}Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n}}\right] ^{2}|\mathcal{F}%
_{n}^{Z}\right) \right\} \\
&\leq &\overline{C}
\end{eqnarray*}%
It follows from Markov's inequality that, for any $\epsilon >0$, we can set $%
C_{\epsilon }=\sqrt{\overline{C}/\epsilon }$ so that, for all $n$
sufficiently large,%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&\Pr \left( \left\vert \frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime
}M^{Q}Z_{1}\left( Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}\right) ^{-1}Z_{1}^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n}}\right\vert \geq C_{\epsilon }\right) \\
&=&\Pr \left( \left\vert \frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime
}M^{Q}Z_{1}\left( Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}\right) ^{-1}Z_{1}^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n}}\right\vert ^{2}\geq C_{\epsilon }^{2}\right) \\
&\leq &\frac{E\left( \left[ a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime
}M^{Q}Z_{1}\left( Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}\right) ^{-1}Z_{1}^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon /\sqrt{n}\right] ^{2}\right) }{C_{\epsilon }^{2}} \\
&\leq &\frac{\overline{C}}{\overline{C}/\epsilon }=\epsilon
\end{eqnarray*}%
which shows that 
\begin{equation*}
\frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}\left(
Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}\right) ^{-1}Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{%
\sqrt{n}}=O_{p}\left( 1\right)
\end{equation*}%
Since the above result holds for all $a\in \mathbb{R}^{d}$ such that $%
\left\Vert a\right\Vert _{2}=1$, we further deduce that 
\begin{equation*}
\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}\left( Z_{1}^{\prime
}M^{Q}Z_{1}\right) ^{-1}Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n}}%
=O_{p}\left( 1\right) \text{,}
\end{equation*}%
as required for part (a).

Turning our attention to part (b), we again let $a\in \mathbb{R}^{d}$ such
that $\left\Vert a\right\Vert _{2}=1$; and note that, by Assumptions 1,
2(i), and 3(iii),%
\begin{eqnarray*}
E\left( \left[ \frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n}}\right] ^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right) &=&%
\frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{Q}E\left[ \varepsilon
\varepsilon ^{\prime }|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] M^{Q}Z_{2}\Upsilon a}{n} \\
&\leq &\left( \max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}E\left[ \varepsilon
_{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \right) \frac{a^{\prime
}\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{2}\Upsilon a}{n} \\
&\leq &\left( \max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}E\left[ \varepsilon
_{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \right) \frac{a^{\prime
}\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }Z_{2}\Upsilon a}{n} \\
&=&O_{a.s.}\left( 1\right)
\end{eqnarray*}%
Hence, there exists a positive constant $\overline{C}<\infty $ such that for
all $n$ sufficiently large%
\begin{equation*}
E\left( \left[ \frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n}}\right] ^{2}\right) =E_{Z}\left\{ E\left( \left[
\frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n%
}}\right] ^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right) \right\} \leq \overline{C}\text{.}
\end{equation*}%
It follows from Markov's inequality, for any $\epsilon >0$, we can set $%
C_{\epsilon }=\sqrt{\overline{C}/\epsilon }$ so that for all $n$
sufficiently large%
\begin{eqnarray*}
\Pr \left( \left\vert \frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n}}\right\vert \geq C_{\epsilon }\right) &=&\Pr
\left( \left\vert \frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n}}\right\vert ^{2}\geq C_{\epsilon }^{2}\right) \\
&\leq &\frac{E\left( \left[ a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon /\sqrt{n}\right] ^{2}\right) }{C_{\epsilon }^{2}} \\
&\leq &\frac{\overline{C}}{\overline{C}/\epsilon }=\epsilon
\end{eqnarray*}%
which shows that%
\begin{equation*}
\frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n%
}}=O_{p}\left( 1\right) .
\end{equation*}%
Since the above result holds for all $a\in \mathbb{R}^{d}$ such that $%
\left\Vert a\right\Vert _{2}=1$, we further deduce that%
\begin{equation*}
\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n}}%
=O_{p}\left( 1\right) \text{.}
\end{equation*}

Finally, for part (c), note that it follows immediately from parts (a) and
(b) above that%
\begin{equation*}
\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n}}=\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n}}-\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime
}M^{Q}Z_{1}\left( Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}\right) ^{-1}Z_{1}^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n}}=O_{p}\left( 1\right) \text{,}
\end{equation*}%
as required. $\square $

\medskip

\noindent \textbf{Lemma OA-3: }

If Assumptions 1, 2(i), 4(ii), 5, and 6(i) are satisfied; then,%
\begin{equation*}
\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }A\varepsilon }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}=O_{p}\left(
1\right) .\text{ }
\end{equation*}

\medskip

\noindent \textbf{Proof of Lemma OA-3: }

To proceed, note that, by the symmetry of $A$ and by Assumptions 1, 2(i),
and 5; we have%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&E\left( \left[ \frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }A\varepsilon }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}%
\right] ^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right) \\
&=&\frac{1}{K_{2,n}}\dsum\limits_{\substack{ \left( i_{1},t_{1}\right)
,\left( j_{1},s_{1}\right) =1  \\ \left( i_{1},t_{1}\right) \neq \left(
j_{1},s_{1}\right) }}^{m_{n}}\dsum\limits_{\substack{ \left(
i_{2},t_{2}\right) ,\left( j_{2},s_{2}\right) =1  \\ \left(
i_{2},t_{2}\right) \neq \left( j_{2},s_{2}\right) }}^{m_{n}}A_{\left(
i_{1},t_{1}\right) ,\left( j_{1},s_{1}\right) }A_{\left( i_{2},t_{2}\right)
,\left( j_{2},s_{2}\right) }E\left[ \varepsilon _{\left( i_{1},t_{1}\right)
}\varepsilon _{\left( j_{1},s_{1}\right) }\varepsilon _{\left(
i_{2},t_{2}\right) }\varepsilon _{\left( j_{2},s_{2}\right) }|\mathcal{F}%
_{n}^{Z}\right] \\
&=&\frac{2}{K_{2,n}}\dsum\limits_{\substack{ \left( i,t\right) ,\left(
j,s\right) =1  \\ \left( i,t\right) \neq \left( j,s\right) }}%
^{m_{n}}A_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( j,s\right) }^{2}E\left[ \varepsilon
_{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}\varepsilon _{\left( j,s\right) }^{2}|\mathcal{F}%
_{n}^{Z}\right] \\
&\leq &2\left( \max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}E\left[ \varepsilon
_{\left( i,t\right) }^{4}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \right) \frac{1}{K_{2,n}%
}\dsum\limits_{\substack{ \left( i,t\right) ,\left( j,s\right) =1  \\ \left(
i,t\right) \neq \left( j,s\right) }}^{m_{n}}A_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left(
j,s\right) }^{2} \\
&=&O_{a.s.}\left( 1\right)
\end{eqnarray*}%
Hence, there exists a positive constant $\overline{C}<\infty $ such that for
all $n$ sufficiently large%
\begin{equation*}
E\left( \left[ \frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }A\varepsilon }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}%
\right] ^{2}\right) =E_{Z}\left\{ E\left( \left[ \frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime
}A\varepsilon }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}\right] ^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right)
\right\} \leq \overline{C}\text{.}
\end{equation*}%
It follows from Markov's inequality, for any $\epsilon >0$, we can set $%
C_{\epsilon }=\sqrt{\overline{C}/\epsilon }$ so that for all $n$
sufficiently large%
\begin{eqnarray*}
\Pr \left( \left\vert \frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }A\varepsilon }{\sqrt{%
K_{2,n}}}\right\vert \geq C_{\epsilon }\right) &=&\Pr \left( \left\vert 
\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }A\varepsilon }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}\right\vert
^{2}\geq C_{\epsilon }^{2}\right) \\
&\leq &\frac{E\left( \left[ \varepsilon ^{\prime }A\varepsilon /\sqrt{K_{2,n}%
}\right] ^{2}\right) }{C_{\epsilon }^{2}} \\
&\leq &\frac{\overline{C}}{\overline{C}/\epsilon }=\epsilon
\end{eqnarray*}%
which shows that%
\begin{equation*}
\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }A\varepsilon }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}=O_{p}\left(
1\right) \text{. }\square
\end{equation*}

\noindent

\medskip

\noindent \textbf{Lemma OA-4: }Under Assumptions 1, 2, 6, and 8; the
following statements are true.

\begin{enumerate}
\item[(a)] 
\begin{equation*}
\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{n}-E\left[ \frac{\varepsilon
^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{n}\right] =O_{p}\left( \frac{1}{\sqrt{n}}%
\right) \text{,}
\end{equation*}%
and there exist positive constants $\underline{C}\leq \overline{C}$ such that%
\begin{equation*}
0<\underline{C}\leq E\left[ \frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{n}%
\right] \leq \overline{C}<\infty
\end{equation*}%
for all $n$ sufficiently large.

\item[(b)] 
\begin{equation*}
\frac{U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon }{n}-E\left[ \frac{%
U^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{n}\right] =O_{p}\left( \max \left\{ \frac{1}{%
\sqrt{n}},\frac{K_{1,n}}{n}\right\} \right) ,
\end{equation*}%
where%
\begin{equation*}
E\left[ \frac{U^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{n}\right] =O\left( 1\right) .
\end{equation*}

\item[(c)] 
\begin{equation*}
\frac{U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon }{\varepsilon
^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }-\rho =O_{p}\left( \max \left\{ \frac{1}{\sqrt{n}%
},\frac{K_{1,n}}{n}\right\} \right) ,
\end{equation*}%
where 
\begin{equation*}
\rho =\lim_{n\rightarrow \infty }\rho _{n}=\lim_{n\rightarrow \infty }\frac{E%
\left[ U^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] /n}{E\left[ \varepsilon ^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] /n}\text{. }
\end{equation*}
\end{enumerate}

\medskip

\noindent \textbf{Proof of Lemma OA-4:} To show part (a), note first that,
making use of Assumptions 1, 2(i), and 6(ii); we have%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&E\left( \frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon -E\left[ \varepsilon
^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] }{n}\right) ^{2} \\
&=&\frac{E\left( \dsum\limits_{i=1}^{n}\dsum\limits_{t=1}^{T_{i}}\left( 
\frac{T_{i}-1}{T_{i}}\right) \left[ \varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right)
}^{2}-E\left\{ \varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}\right\} \right]
-\dsum\limits_{i=1}^{n}\frac{1}{T_{i}}\dsum\limits_{r=1}^{T_{i}}\dsum\limits 
_{\substack{ s=1  \\ s\neq r}}^{T_{i}}\varepsilon _{\left( i,r\right)
}\varepsilon _{\left( i,s\right) }\right) ^{2}}{n^{2}} \\
&=&\frac{1}{n^{2}}\dsum\limits_{i=1}^{n}\dsum\limits_{t=1}^{T_{i}}\dsum%
\limits_{j=1}^{n}\dsum\limits_{s=1}^{T_{j}}\left( \frac{T_{i}-1}{T_{i}}%
\right) \left( \frac{T_{j}-1}{T_{j}}\right) E\left( \left[ \varepsilon
_{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}-E\left\{ \varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right)
}^{2}\right\} \right] \left[ \varepsilon _{\left( j,s\right) }^{2}-E\left\{
\varepsilon _{\left( j,s\right) }^{2}\right\} \right] \right) \\
&&-\frac{2}{n^{2}}\dsum\limits_{i=1}^{n}\dsum\limits_{t=1}^{T_{i}}\dsum%
\limits_{j=1}^{n}\dsum\limits_{r=1}^{T_{j}}\dsum\limits_{\substack{ s=1  \\ %
s\neq r}}^{T_{j}}\left( \frac{T_{i}-1}{T_{i}}\right) \frac{1}{T_{j}}E\left\{ %
\left[ \varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}-E\left\{ \varepsilon _{\left(
i,t\right) }^{2}\right\} \right] \varepsilon _{\left( j,r\right)
}\varepsilon _{\left( j,s\right) }\right\} \\
&&+\frac{1}{n^{2}}\dsum\limits_{i=1}^{n}\dsum\limits_{t=1}^{T_{i}}\dsum%
\limits_{\substack{ s=1  \\ s\neq t}}^{T_{i}}\dsum\limits_{j=1}^{n}\dsum%
\limits_{r=1}^{T_{j}}\dsum\limits_{\substack{ h=1  \\ h\neq r}}%
^{T_{j}}\left( \frac{1}{T_{i}}\right) \left( \frac{1}{T_{j}}\right) E\left[
\varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right) }\varepsilon _{\left( i,s\right)
}\varepsilon _{\left( j,r\right) }\varepsilon _{\left( j,h\right) }\right] \\
&=&\frac{1}{n^{2}}\dsum\limits_{i=1}^{n}\dsum\limits_{t=1}^{T_{i}}\dsum%
\limits_{j=1}^{n}\dsum\limits_{s=1}^{T_{j}}\left( \frac{T_{i}-1}{T_{i}}%
\right) \left( \frac{T_{j}-1}{T_{j}}\right) E\left( \left[ \varepsilon
_{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}-E\left\{ \varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right)
}^{2}\right\} \right] \left[ \varepsilon _{\left( j,s\right) }^{2}-E\left\{
\varepsilon _{\left( j,s\right) }^{2}\right\} \right] \right) \\
&&+\frac{2}{n^{2}}\dsum\limits_{i=1}^{n}\dsum\limits_{t=1}^{T_{i}}\dsum%
\limits_{\substack{ s=1  \\ s\neq t}}^{T_{i}}\left( \frac{1}{T_{i}}\right)
^{2}E\left[ \varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}\right] E\left[ \varepsilon
_{\left( i,s\right) }^{2}\right] \\
&=&\frac{1}{n^{2}}\dsum\limits_{i=1}^{n}\dsum\limits_{t=1}^{T_{i}}\left( 
\frac{T_{i}-1}{T_{i}}\right) ^{2}E\left( \varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right)
}^{2}-E\left\{ \varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}\right\} \right) ^{2}+%
\frac{2}{n^{2}}\dsum\limits_{i=1}^{n}\dsum\limits_{t=1}^{T_{i}}\dsum\limits 
_{\substack{ s=1  \\ s\neq t}}^{T_{i}}\left( \frac{1}{T_{i}}\right) ^{2}E%
\left[ \varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}\right] E\left[ \varepsilon
_{\left( i,s\right) }^{2}\right] \\
&\leq &\frac{1}{n^{2}}n\overline{T}\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}E%
\left[ \varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right) }^{4}\right] +\frac{2}{n^{2}}n\left(
\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}E\left[ \varepsilon _{\left(
i,t\right) }^{2}\right] \right) ^{2} \\
&=&\frac{1}{n}\overline{T}\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}E\left[
\varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right) }^{4}\right] +\frac{2}{n}\left( \max_{1\leq
\left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}E\left[ \varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}%
\right] \right) ^{2} \\
&=&O\left( \frac{1}{n}\right)
\end{eqnarray*}%
It follows by Markov's inequality that 
\begin{equation}
\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon -E\left[ \varepsilon ^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] }{n}=O_{p}\left( \frac{1}{\sqrt{n}}\right) \text{. 
}  \label{eMZ1Qe}
\end{equation}%
Next, note that, by Assumption 6(i), $T_{i}\geq 3$ for all $i$, so that $%
\frac{T_{i}-1}{T_{i}}\geq \frac{2}{3}$ \ for all $i$. Hence, by Assumption
2(ii), there exists a positive contant $\underline{C}$ such that $E\left[
\varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \geq 
\underline{C}>0$ $a.s.$, so that%
\begin{eqnarray*}
\frac{E\left[ \varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] }{n} &=&\frac{1%
}{n}E_{Z}\left\{ \dsum\limits_{i=1}^{n}\dsum\limits_{t=1}^{T_{i}}\left[
\left( \frac{T_{i}-1}{T_{i}}\right) \right] E\left[ \varepsilon _{\left(
i,t\right) }^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \right\} \\
&\geq &\frac{2}{3n}E_{Z}\left\{
\dsum\limits_{i=1}^{n}\dsum\limits_{t=1}^{T_{i}}E\left[ \varepsilon _{\left(
i,t\right) }^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \right\} \\
&\geq &\frac{2}{3n}E_{Z}\left[ \dsum\limits_{i=1}^{n}\dsum%
\limits_{t=1}^{T_{i}}\underline{C}\right] \\
&=&\frac{2}{3n}E_{Z}\left[ \dsum\limits_{\left( i,t\right) =1}^{m_{n}}%
\underline{C}\right] \\
&=&\frac{2}{3}\frac{m_{n}}{n}\underline{C} \\
&\geq &\frac{2}{3}\underline{C}>0
\end{eqnarray*}%
for all $n$ sufficiently large. Furthermore, by Assumption 2(i), there also
exists a positive contant $C$ $\left( \geq \underline{C}\right) $ such that%
\begin{equation*}
\left( \max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}E\left[ \varepsilon _{\left(
i,t\right) }^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \right) \leq C\text{ }a.s.\text{,%
}
\end{equation*}%
from which it follows that%
\begin{eqnarray*}
E\left[ \frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{n}\right] &=&\frac{1}{%
n}E_{Z}\left\{ \dsum\limits_{i=1}^{n}\dsum\limits_{t=1}^{T_{i}}\left( \frac{%
T_{i}-1}{T_{i}}\right) E\left[ \varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}|%
\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \right\} \\
&\leq &\frac{1}{n}E_{Z}\left\{
\dsum\limits_{i=1}^{n}\dsum\limits_{t=1}^{T_{i}}E\left[ \varepsilon _{\left(
i,t\right) }^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \right\} \\
&\leq &\frac{m_{n}}{n}C=\overline{C}<\infty \text{. }
\end{eqnarray*}

Next, to show part (b), let $b\in \mathbb{R}^{d}$ such that $\left\Vert
b\right\Vert _{2}=1$; and since $M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}=M^{Q}-P^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}$, where $P^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}=M^{Q}Z_{1}\left(
Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}\right) ^{-1}Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}$, we can write%
\begin{equation*}
\frac{b^{\prime }U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon }{n}=\frac{%
b^{\prime }U^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{n}-\frac{b^{\prime }U^{\prime
}P^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}\varepsilon }{n}\text{. }
\end{equation*}%
Note first that by argument similar to that given in part (a) above, we can
show that%
\begin{equation}
\frac{b^{\prime }U^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{n}-E\left[ \frac{b^{\prime
}U^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{n}\right] =O_{p}\left( \frac{1}{\sqrt{n}}%
\right) \text{.}  \label{bUMe}
\end{equation}

Next, note that, by application of the CS inequality and Assumptions 1,
2(i), and 5; we have%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&E\left[ \left\vert \frac{b^{\prime }U^{\prime }P^{Z_{1}^{\perp
}}\varepsilon }{n}\right\vert |\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \\
&\leq &\sqrt{E\left[ \frac{b^{\prime }U^{\prime }P^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}Ub}{n}|%
\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] }\sqrt{E\left[ \frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime
}P^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}\varepsilon }{n}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] } \\
&=&\sqrt{\frac{1}{n}\dsum\limits_{\left( i,t\right)
=1}^{m_{n}}\dsum\limits_{\left( j,s\right) =1}^{m_{n}}P_{\left( i,t\right)
,\left( j,s\right) }^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}b^{\prime }E\left[ U_{\left( i,t\right)
}U_{\left( j,s\right) }^{\prime }|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] b}\sqrt{\frac{1%
}{n}\dsum\limits_{\left( i,t\right) =1}^{m_{n}}\dsum\limits_{\left(
j,s\right) =1}^{m_{n}}P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( j,s\right)
}^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}E\left[ \varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right) }\varepsilon
_{\left( j,s\right) }|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] } \\
&=&\sqrt{\frac{1}{n}\dsum\limits_{\left( i,t\right) =1}^{m_{n}}P_{\left(
i,t\right) ,\left( i,t\right) }^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}b^{\prime }E\left[ U_{\left(
i,t\right) }U_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime }|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] b}%
\sqrt{\frac{1}{n}\dsum\limits_{\left( i,t\right) =1}^{m_{n}}P_{\left(
i,t\right) ,\left( i,t\right) }^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}E\left[ \varepsilon _{\left(
i,t\right) }^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] } \\
&\leq &\sqrt{\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}E\left[ \left\Vert
U_{\left( i,t\right) }\right\Vert _{2}^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] }\sqrt{%
\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}E\left[ \varepsilon _{\left(
i,t\right) }^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] }\frac{K_{1,n}}{n}%
=O_{a.s.}\left( \frac{K_{1,n}}{n}\right)
\end{eqnarray*}%
Hence, there exists a constant $\overline{C}<\infty $ such that for all $n$
sufficiently large 
\begin{equation*}
E\left[ \frac{n}{K_{1,n}}\left\vert \frac{b^{\prime }U^{\prime
}P^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}\varepsilon }{n}\right\vert \right] =E_{Z}\left( E\left[ 
\frac{n}{K_{1,n}}\left\vert \frac{b^{\prime }U^{\prime }P^{Z_{1}^{\perp
}}\varepsilon }{n}\right\vert |\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \right) \leq 
\overline{C}\text{. \ }
\end{equation*}%
Application of Markov's inequality then implies that for any $\epsilon >0$, 
\begin{equation*}
\Pr \left( \frac{n}{K_{1,n}}\left\vert \frac{b^{\prime }U^{\prime
}P^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}\varepsilon }{n}\right\vert \geq \frac{\overline{C}}{%
\epsilon }\right) \leq \epsilon \frac{n}{K_{1,n}}\frac{E\left[ \left\vert
b^{\prime }U^{\prime }P^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}\varepsilon /n\right\vert \right] }{%
\overline{C}}\leq \epsilon
\end{equation*}%
for all $n$ sufficiently large, which shows that%
\begin{equation}
\frac{b^{\prime }U^{\prime }P^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}\varepsilon }{n}=O_{p}\left( 
\frac{K_{1,n}}{n}\right) .  \label{bUPZ1e}
\end{equation}%
It follows from (\ref{bUMe}) and (\ref{bUPZ1e}) that%
\begin{equation*}
\frac{b^{\prime }U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon }{n}-E%
\left[ \frac{b^{\prime }U^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{n}\right] =O_{p}\left(
\max \left\{ \frac{1}{\sqrt{n}},\frac{K_{1,n}}{n}\right\} \right)
\end{equation*}

In addition, by the CS inequality and Assumptions 2(i) and 6(ii),%
\begin{eqnarray*}
\left\vert \frac{E\left[ b^{\prime }U^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] }{n}%
\right\vert &=&\frac{1}{n}\left\vert
\dsum\limits_{i=1}^{n}\dsum\limits_{t=1}^{T_{i}}\left( \frac{T_{i}-1}{T_{i}}%
\right) E\left[ b^{\prime }U_{\left( i,t\right) }\varepsilon _{\left(
i,t\right) }\right] \right\vert \\
&\leq &\frac{1}{n}\dsum\limits_{i=1}^{n}\dsum\limits_{t=1}^{T_{i}}E\left[
\left\vert b^{\prime }U_{\left( i,t\right) }\varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right)
}\right\vert \right] \\
&\leq &\frac{1}{n}\dsum\limits_{i=1}^{n}\dsum\limits_{t=1}^{T_{i}}\sqrt{%
b^{\prime }E\left[ U_{\left( i,t\right) }U_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime }%
\right] b}\sqrt{E\left[ \varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}\right] } \\
&\leq &\overline{T}\sqrt{\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq
m_{n}}E\left\Vert U_{\left( i,t\right) }\right\Vert ^{2}}\sqrt{\max_{1\leq
\left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}E\left[ \varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}%
\right] } \\
&=&O\left( 1\right)
\end{eqnarray*}%
Since the above argument holds for any $b\in \mathbb{R}^{d}$ such that $%
\left\Vert b\right\Vert _{2}=1$, we further deduce that%
\begin{equation*}
\frac{U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon }{n}-E\left[ \frac{%
U^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{n}\right] =O_{p}\left( \max \left\{ \frac{1}{%
\sqrt{n}},\frac{K_{1,n}}{n}\right\} \right) \text{. }
\end{equation*}%
and%
\begin{equation*}
E\left[ \frac{U^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{n}\right] =O\left( 1\right) 
\text{,}
\end{equation*}%
as required to show part (b).

Finally, to show part (c), we first write%
\begin{equation*}
\frac{U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon }{\varepsilon
^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }-\rho =\frac{U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}\varepsilon }{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }-\rho _{n}+\rho
_{n}-\rho
\end{equation*}%
By Assumption 8, the sequence $\left\{ \rho _{n}\right\} $ has a limit
defined to be $\rho $ so that $\rho _{n}-\rho \rightarrow 0$ as $%
n\rightarrow \infty $. Next, note that 
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&\frac{U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon }{\varepsilon
^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }-\rho _{n} \\
&=&\frac{U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon }{\varepsilon
^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }-\frac{E\left[ U^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon %
\right] }{E\left[ \varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] } \\
&=&\frac{U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon }{E\left[
\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] }-\frac{E\left[ U^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] }{E\left[ \varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon %
\right] }+\frac{U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon }{%
\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }-\frac{U^{\prime }M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon }{E\left[ \varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon %
\right] } \\
&=&\frac{U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon -E\left[ U^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] }{E\left[ \varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon %
\right] }+\frac{U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon E\left[
\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] }{\left( \varepsilon ^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon \right) E\left[ \varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon %
\right] }-\frac{\left( \varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \right)
U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon }{\left( \varepsilon
^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \right) E\left[ \varepsilon ^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] } \\
&=&\frac{U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon -E\left[ U^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] }{E\left[ \varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon %
\right] }-\frac{U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon }{%
\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }\frac{\left( \varepsilon ^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon -E\left[ \varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \right]
\right) }{E\left[ \varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] }
\end{eqnarray*}%
Now, applying the results of parts (a) and (b) above and the Slutsky's
theorem, we obtain%
\begin{eqnarray*}
\frac{U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon -E\left[ U^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] }{E\left[ \varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon %
\right] } &=&\frac{\left( U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon -E%
\left[ U^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] \right) /n}{E\left[ \varepsilon
^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] /n}=O_{p}\left( \max \left\{ \frac{1}{%
\sqrt{n}},\frac{K_{1,n}}{n}\right\} \right) , \\
\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon -E\left[ \varepsilon ^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] }{E\left[ \varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon %
\right] } &=&\frac{\left( \varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon -E\left[
\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] \right) /n}{E\left[
\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] /n}=O_{p}\left( \frac{1}{%
\sqrt{n}}\right) ,
\end{eqnarray*}%
and

\begin{eqnarray*}
\frac{U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon }{\varepsilon
^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon } &=&\frac{U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}\varepsilon /n}{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon /n} \\
&=&\frac{\left( U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon -E\left[
U^{\prime }M^{,Q}\varepsilon \right] \right) /n+E\left[ U^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] /n}{\left( \varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon
-E\left[ \varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] \right) /n+E\left[
\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] /n} \\
&=&\frac{E\left[ U^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] /n+o_{p}(1)}{E\left[
\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] /n+o_{p}(1)}=O_{p}\left(
1\right) \text{.}
\end{eqnarray*}%
It follows that%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&\frac{U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon }{\varepsilon
^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }-\rho _{n} \\
&=&\frac{U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon }{\varepsilon
^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }-\frac{E\left[ U^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon %
\right] }{E\left[ \varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] } \\
&=&\frac{\left( U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon -E\left[
U^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] \right) /n}{E\left[ \varepsilon ^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] /n}-\frac{U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}\varepsilon }{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }\frac{\varepsilon
^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon -E\left[ \varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon %
\right] /n}{E\left[ \varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \right] /n} \\
&=&O_{p}\left( \max \left\{ \frac{1}{\sqrt{n}},\frac{K_{1,n}}{n}\right\}
\right) -O_{p}\left( 1\right) O_{p}\left( \frac{1}{\sqrt{n}}\right) \\
&=&O_{p}\left( \max \left\{ \frac{1}{\sqrt{n}},\frac{K_{1,n}}{n}\right\}
\right) \text{. }\square
\end{eqnarray*}

\medskip

\noindent \textbf{Lemma OA-5: }

Suppose that Assumptions 1-6 are satisfied. Let 
\begin{equation*}
\widehat{\ell }\left( \delta _{0}\right) =\frac{\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right)
^{\prime }A\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) }{\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right)
^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) }\text{;}
\end{equation*}%
then,%
\begin{equation*}
\widehat{\ell }\left( \delta _{0}\right) =\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime
}A\varepsilon }{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }\left[ 1+O_{p}\left(
\max \left\{ \frac{\tau _{n}}{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}K_{1,n}^{\varrho _{g}}},\frac{%
K_{1,n}}{n}\right\} \right) \right] \text{,}
\end{equation*}

\bigskip

\noindent \textbf{Proof of Lemma OA-5:}

To proceed, first write%
\begin{equation*}
\widehat{\ell }\left( \delta _{0}\right) =\frac{\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right)
^{\prime }A\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) }{\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right)
^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) }=\frac{%
\varepsilon ^{\prime }A\varepsilon }{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon }
\end{equation*}%
Moreover, note that $\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}\varepsilon /n=\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon \NEG{/}n-\varepsilon
^{\prime }P^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}\varepsilon /n$. By the results of part (a) of
Lemma OA-4, we have that $\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon /n-E\left[
\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon /n\right] =O_{p}\left(
n^{-1/2}\right) $, and also that there exist positive constants $\underline{C%
}\leq \overline{C}$ such that, for all $n$ sufficiently large, $0<\underline{%
C}\leq E\left[ \varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon /n\right] \leq 
\overline{C}<\infty $. In addition, by argument similar to that used to
obtain expression (\ref{bUPZ1e}) in the proof of part (b) of Lemma OA-4, we
can show that $\varepsilon ^{\prime }P^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}\varepsilon
/n=O_{p}\left( K_{1,n}/n\right) =o_{p}\left( 1\right) $. It follows that%
\begin{equation}
\frac{\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) }{n}=\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon }{n}=\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon }{n}\left[ 1+O_{p}\left( \frac{K_{1,n}}{n}\right) \right] 
\text{,}  \label{residMresid}
\end{equation}%
where $\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon /n=O_{p}\left( 1\right) $ and
where $\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon /n>0$ w.p.a.1. Finally, note
that%
\begin{eqnarray*}
\widehat{\ell }\left( \delta _{0}\right) &=&\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime
}A\varepsilon }{n}\left[ \frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon }{n}\right] ^{-1} \\
&=&\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }A\varepsilon }{n}\left[ \frac{\varepsilon
^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{n}\left( 1+O_{p}\left( \frac{K_{1,n}}{n}\right)
\right) \right] ^{-1} \\
&=&\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }A\varepsilon }{\varepsilon ^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon }\left[ 1+O_{p}\left( \frac{K_{1,n}}{n}\right) \right]
^{-1} \\
&=&\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }A\varepsilon }{\varepsilon ^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon }\left[ 1+O_{p}\left( \frac{K_{1,n}}{n}\right) \right]
\end{eqnarray*}%
which shows the required result. $\square $

\medskip

\noindent \textbf{Lemma OA-6: }Suppose that Assumptions 1-6 are satisfied.
Let $\widehat{\delta }_{n}$ be any estimator that satisfies the following
conditions as $n\rightarrow \infty $

\begin{enumerate}
\item[(i)] If $K_{2,n}/\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) ^{2}=O\left( 1\right) $%
, then%
\begin{equation*}
D_{\mu }\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) =O_{p}\left( 1\right)
\end{equation*}

\item[(ii)] If $\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) ^{2}/K_{2,n}=o\left( 1\right) 
$ but $\sqrt{K_{2,n}}/\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) ^{2}\rightarrow 0$, then%
\begin{equation*}
\frac{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) D_{\mu }\left( \widehat{\delta }%
_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}=O_{p}\left( 1\right)
\end{equation*}
\end{enumerate}

\noindent Under these conditions, the following statements are true.

\begin{enumerate}
\item[(a)] Under case (i),%
\begin{equation*}
D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }A\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) =O_{p}\left(
1\right)
\end{equation*}%
while, under case (ii), 
\begin{equation*}
D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }A\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) =O_{p}\left( 
\frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\right) \text{.}
\end{equation*}

\item[(b)] Under both case (i)\ and case (ii),%
\begin{equation*}
D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }%
_{n}\right) =O_{p}\left( \frac{n}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\right)
\end{equation*}

\item[(c)] Under both case (i) and case (ii),%
\begin{equation*}
\frac{\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) ^{\prime }A\left( y-X\widehat{%
\delta }_{n}\right) }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}=\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime
}A\varepsilon }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}+o_{p}\left( 1\right) \text{,}
\end{equation*}%
where $\varepsilon ^{\prime }A\varepsilon /\sqrt{K_{2,n}}=O_{p}\left(
1\right) $.

\item[(d)] Under both case (i) and case (ii),%
\begin{equation*}
\frac{\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) ^{\prime }M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) }{n}=\frac{%
\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{n}\left[ 1+o_{p}\left( 1\right) %
\right] ,
\end{equation*}%
where $\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon /n=O_{p}\left( 1\right) $ and
where $\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon /n>0$ w.p.a.1.

\item[(e)] Under both case (i) and case (ii),%
\begin{equation*}
\widehat{\ell }\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) =\frac{\varepsilon
^{\prime }A\varepsilon }{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }%
+o_{p}\left( \frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{n}\right) =O_{p}\left( \frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}%
}}{n}\right) \text{,}
\end{equation*}%
where%
\begin{equation*}
\widehat{\ell }\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) =\frac{\left( y-X\widehat{%
\delta }_{n}\right) ^{\prime }A\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) }{%
\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) ^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) }\text{.}
\end{equation*}
\end{enumerate}

\bigskip

\noindent \textbf{Proof of Lemma OA-6:}

To show part (a), note that%
\begin{eqnarray}
D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }A\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) &=&D_{\mu
}^{-1}X^{\prime }A\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) +D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime
}AX\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right)  \notag \\
&=&D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }A\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) +D_{\mu
}^{-1}X^{\prime }AXD_{\mu }^{-1}D_{\mu }\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta
_{0}\right)  \label{DXAresid}
\end{eqnarray}%
To analyze the first term on the right-hand side of expression (\ref%
{DXAresid}) above, write%
\begin{equation*}
D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }A\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) =\frac{\Upsilon
^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n}}%
+D_{\mu }^{-1}U^{\prime }A\varepsilon
\end{equation*}%
Now, consider case (i) where $\sqrt{K_{2,n}}/\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right)
=O\left( 1\right) $. In this case, we have by part (c) of Lemma OA-2 and
expression (\ref{OAe 3}) that%
\begin{equation*}
\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n}}=O_{p}\left( 1\right) \text{ and }D_{\mu
}^{-1}U^{\prime }A\varepsilon =O_{p}\left( \frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{\left( \mu
_{n}^{\min }\right) }\right) \text{,}
\end{equation*}%
from which it follows that, in this case, $D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }A\left(
y-X\delta _{0}\right) =O_{p}\left( 1\right) $. In addition, by part (b) of
Lemma S2-2, we have in this case 
\begin{equation*}
D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }AXD_{\mu }^{-1}D_{\mu }\left( \widehat{\delta }%
_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) =O_{p}\left( 1\right) \text{,}
\end{equation*}%
so that, in this case, 
\begin{eqnarray*}
D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }A\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) &=&D_{\mu
}^{-1}X^{\prime }A\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) +D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime
}AXD_{\mu }^{-1}D_{\mu }\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) \\
&=&O_{p}\left( 1\right) +O_{p}\left( 1\right) =O_{p}\left( 1\right)
\end{eqnarray*}%
Next, consider case (ii) where $\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) /\sqrt{K_{2,n}%
}=o\left( 1\right) $ but$\sqrt{K_{2,n}}/\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right)
^{2}\rightarrow 0$. Here, again by part (c) of Lemma OA-2, and expression (%
\ref{OAe 3}), we have 
\begin{equation*}
D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }A\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) =O_{p}\left( \frac{%
\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\right)
\end{equation*}%
Furthermore, in this case, we also have, by using part (b) of Lemma S2-2 
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }AXD_{\mu }^{-1}D_{\mu }\left( \widehat{\delta }%
_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) \\
&=&\frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }D_{\mu
}^{-1}X^{\prime }AXD_{\mu }^{-1}\frac{\mu _{n}^{\min }D_{\mu }\left( 
\widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}=O_{p}\left( \frac{%
\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\right)
\end{eqnarray*}%
from which it follows that in case (ii)%
\begin{eqnarray*}
D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }A\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) &=&D_{\mu
}^{-1}X^{\prime }A\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) +D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime
}AXD_{\mu }^{-1}D_{\mu }\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) \\
&=&O_{p}\left( \frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\right)
+O_{p}\left( \frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\right) \\
&=&O_{p}\left( \frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\right) 
\text{.}
\end{eqnarray*}

Next, consider part (b). In this case, note that%
\begin{eqnarray}
&&D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\left( y-X\widehat{%
\delta }_{n}\right)  \notag \\
&=&D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\left( y-X\delta
_{0}\right) +D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }X\left( 
\widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right)  \notag \\
&=&D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\left( y-X\delta
_{0}\right) +D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }XD_{\mu
}^{-1}D_{\mu }\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right)
\label{DXMresid}
\end{eqnarray}%
The first term on the right-hand side of the expression (\ref{DXMresid})
above can be written as%
\begin{equation*}
D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\left( y-X\delta
_{0}\right) =D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon =%
\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n}}+D_{\mu }^{-1}U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}\varepsilon
\end{equation*}%
Now, consider case (i) where $\sqrt{K_{2,n}}/\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right)
=O\left( 1\right) $. In this case, we have by part (c) of Lemma OA-2 and
expression (\ref{UMZ1Qe}) that 
\begin{equation*}
\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}\varepsilon }{\sqrt{n}}=O_{p}\left( 1\right) \text{ and }D_{\mu
}^{-1}U^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon =O_{p}\left( \frac{n}{%
\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\right) \text{,}
\end{equation*}%
from which it follows that, in this case, 
\begin{equation*}
D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\left( y-X\delta
_{0}\right) =O_{p}\left( \frac{n}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\right) .
\end{equation*}%
In addition, by part (a) of Lemma S2-2, we have in this case%
\begin{equation*}
D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }XD_{\mu }^{-1}D_{\mu
}\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) =O_{p}\left( \frac{n}{%
\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) ^{2}}\right) \text{,}
\end{equation*}%
so that, in this case, 
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\left( y-X\widehat{%
\delta }_{n}\right) \\
&=&D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\left( y-X\delta
_{0}\right) +D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }XD_{\mu
}^{-1}D_{\mu }\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) \\
&=&O_{p}\left( \frac{n}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\right) +O_{p}\left( 
\frac{n}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) ^{2}}\right) =O_{p}\left( \frac{n}{%
\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\right)
\end{eqnarray*}%
Next, consider case (ii) where $\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) /\sqrt{K_{2,n}%
}=o\left( 1\right) $ but$\sqrt{K_{2,n}}/\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right)
^{2}\rightarrow 0$. Here, again by part (c) of Lemma OA-2 and expression (%
\ref{UMZ1Qe}), we have 
\begin{equation*}
D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\left( y-X\delta
_{0}\right) =O_{p}\left( \frac{n}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\right)
\end{equation*}%
Furthermore, using part (a) of Lemma S2-2, we have%
\begin{eqnarray*}
D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }XD_{\mu }^{-1}D_{\mu
}\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) &=&\frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{%
\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }XD_{\mu }^{-1}\frac{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) D_{\mu
}\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}} \\
&=&O_{p}\left( \frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}n}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) ^{3}}%
\right)
\end{eqnarray*}%
from which it follows that in case (ii)%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\left( y-X\widehat{%
\delta }_{n}\right) \\
&=&D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\left( y-X\delta
_{0}\right) +D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }XD_{\mu
}^{-1}D_{\mu }\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) \\
&=&O_{p}\left( \frac{n}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\right) +O_{p}\left( 
\frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}n}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) ^{3}}\right)
=O_{p}\left( \frac{n}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\right)
\end{eqnarray*}%
Combining the results for cases (i) and (ii), we have 
\begin{equation*}
D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }%
_{n}\right) =O_{p}\left( \frac{n}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\right)
\end{equation*}

Consider now part (c). Write%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&\frac{\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) ^{\prime }A\left( y-X\widehat{%
\delta }_{n}\right) }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}} \\
&=&\frac{\left[ y-X\delta _{0}-X\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta
_{0}\right) \right] ^{\prime }A\left[ y-X\delta _{0}-X\left( \widehat{\delta 
}_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) \right] }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}} \\
&=&\frac{\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }A\left( y-X\delta
_{0}\right) }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}-2\frac{\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime
}AX\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}} \\
&&+\frac{\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }X^{\prime
}AX\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}} \\
&=&\frac{\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }A\left( y-X\delta
_{0}\right) }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}-2\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime
}AXD_{\mu }^{-1}\frac{D_{\mu }\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta
_{0}\right) }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}} \\
&&+\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }D_{\mu }\frac{%
D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }AXD_{\mu }^{-1}}{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}D_{\mu }\left( 
\widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right)
\end{eqnarray*}%
Note first that%
\begin{eqnarray*}
\frac{\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }A\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) }{%
\sqrt{K_{2,n}}} &=&\frac{\left( Z_{1}\gamma \tau _{n}/\sqrt{n}+Q\alpha
+\varepsilon \right) ^{\prime }A\left( Z_{1}\gamma \tau _{n}/\sqrt{n}%
+Q\alpha +\varepsilon \right) }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}} \\
&=&\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }A\varepsilon }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}.
\end{eqnarray*}%
and%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }AXD_{\mu }^{-1} \\
&=&\left( Z_{1}\gamma \tau _{n}/\sqrt{n}+Q\alpha +\varepsilon \right)
^{\prime }A\left( Z_{1}\Theta D_{\kappa }/\sqrt{n}+Z_{2}\Upsilon D_{\mu }/%
\sqrt{n}+Q\Xi +U\right) D_{\mu }^{-1} \\
&=&\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }Z_{2}\Upsilon }{%
\sqrt{n}}+\varepsilon ^{\prime }AUD_{\mu }^{-1}
\end{eqnarray*}%
Now, consider case (i) where $\sqrt{K_{2,n}}/\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right)
=O\left( 1\right) $. In this case, we have by part (c) of Lemma OA-2 and
expression (\ref{OAe 3}) that%
\begin{equation*}
\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }Z_{2}\Upsilon }{\sqrt{n%
}}=O_{p}\left( 1\right) \text{ and }\varepsilon ^{\prime }AUD_{\mu
}^{-1}=O_{p}\left( \frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }%
\right) \text{,}
\end{equation*}%
so that $\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }AXD_{\mu }^{-1}=O_{p}\left(
1\right) $ and, thus,%
\begin{equation*}
\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }AXD_{\mu }^{-1}\frac{D_{\mu }\left( 
\widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}=O_{p}\left( \frac{%
1}{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}\right) =o_{p}\left( 1\right)
\end{equation*}%
In addition, by part (b) of Lemma S2-2, we have in this case 
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }D_{\mu }\frac{%
D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }AXD_{\mu }^{-1}}{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}D_{\mu }\left( 
\widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) \\
&=&\frac{1}{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right)
^{\prime }D_{\mu }D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }AXD_{\mu }^{-1}D_{\mu }\left( 
\widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) \\
&=&O_{p}\left( \frac{1}{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}\right) =o_{p}\left( 1\right) \text{,}
\end{eqnarray*}%
from which it follows that%
\begin{eqnarray*}
\frac{\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) ^{\prime }A\left( y-X\widehat{%
\delta }_{n}\right) }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}} &=&\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime
}A\varepsilon }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}+O_{p}\left( \frac{1}{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}\right)
+O_{p}\left( \frac{1}{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}\right) \\
&=&\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }A\varepsilon }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}+o_{p}\left(
1\right) .
\end{eqnarray*}

\noindent Next, consider case (ii) where $\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) /%
\sqrt{K_{2,n}}=o\left( 1\right) $ but$\sqrt{K_{2,n}}/\left( \mu _{n}^{\min
}\right) ^{2}\rightarrow 0$. Here, again by part (c) of Lemma OA-2, and
expression (\ref{OAe 3}), we have 
\begin{equation*}
\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }AXD_{\mu }^{-1}=O_{p}\left( \frac{%
\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\right)
\end{equation*}%
so that%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }AXD_{\mu }^{-1}\frac{D_{\mu }\left( 
\widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}} \\
&=&\frac{1}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right)
^{\prime }AXD_{\mu }^{-1}\frac{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) D_{\mu }\left( 
\widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}} \\
&=&O_{p}\left( \frac{1}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\right) O_{p}\left( 
\frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\right) O_{p}\left(
1\right) =O_{p}\left( \frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right)
^{2}}\right) =o_{p}\left( 1\right) .
\end{eqnarray*}%
Furthermore, in this case, 
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }D_{\mu }\frac{%
D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }AXD_{\mu }^{-1}}{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}D_{\mu }\left( 
\widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) \\
&=&\frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) ^{2}}\left[ \frac{%
\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) \left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta
_{0}\right) ^{\prime }D_{\mu }}{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime
}AXD_{\mu }^{-1}\frac{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) D_{\mu }\left( \widehat{%
\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}\right] \\
&=&O_{p}\left( \frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) ^{2}}%
\right) =o_{p}\left( 1\right)
\end{eqnarray*}%
from which it follows that in case (ii)%
\begin{eqnarray*}
\frac{\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) ^{\prime }A\left( y-X\widehat{%
\delta }_{n}\right) }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}} &=&\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime
}A\varepsilon }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}+O_{p}\left( \frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{\left( \mu
_{n}^{\min }\right) ^{2}}\right) +O_{p}\left( \frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{\left(
\mu _{n}^{\min }\right) ^{2}}\right) \\
&=&\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }A\varepsilon }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}+o_{p}\left(
1\right) \text{.}
\end{eqnarray*}%
Combining the results for cases (i) and (ii), we have%
\begin{equation*}
\frac{\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) ^{\prime }A\left( y-X\widehat{%
\delta }_{n}\right) }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}=\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime
}A\varepsilon }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}+o_{p}\left( 1\right) \text{. }
\end{equation*}%
where $\varepsilon ^{\prime }A\varepsilon /\sqrt{K_{2,n}}=O_{p}\left(
1\right) $ by Lemma OA-3.

Turning our attention to part (d), note that%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&\frac{\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) ^{\prime }M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) }{n} \\
&=&\frac{\left[ y-X\delta _{0}-X\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta
_{0}\right) \right] ^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\left[ y-X\delta
_{0}-X\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) \right] }{n} \\
&=&\frac{\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) }{n}-2\frac{\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right)
^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }X\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta
_{0}\right) }{n} \\
&&+\frac{\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }X^{\prime
}M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }X\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) 
}{n} \\
&=&\frac{\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) }{n}-2\frac{\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right)
^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }XD_{\mu }^{-1}}{n}D_{\mu }\left( 
\widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) \\
&&+\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }D_{\mu }\frac{%
D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }XD_{\mu }^{-1}}{n}D_{\mu
}\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) .
\end{eqnarray*}

\noindent Making use of the arguement used to derive expression (\ref%
{residMresid}) in the proof of Lemma OA-5, we see that%
\begin{equation*}
\frac{\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) }{n}=\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }\varepsilon }{n}=\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon }{n}+O_{p}\left( \frac{K_{1,n}}{n}\right) \text{.}
\end{equation*}

\noindent Moreover, we can write%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }XD_{\mu
}^{-1} \\
&=&\left( Z_{1}\gamma \tau _{n}/\sqrt{n}+Q\alpha +\varepsilon \right)
^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\left( Z_{1}\Theta D_{\kappa }/\sqrt{n}%
+Z_{2}\Upsilon D_{\mu }/\sqrt{n}+Q\Xi +U\right) D_{\mu }^{-1} \\
&=&\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }Z_{2}\Upsilon }{%
\sqrt{n}}+\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }UD_{\mu }^{-1}
\end{eqnarray*}%
Now, consider case (i) where $\sqrt{K_{2,n}}/\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right)
=O\left( 1\right) $. In this case, we have by part (c) of Lemma OA-2 and
expression (\ref{UMZ1Qe}) that%
\begin{equation*}
\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }Z_{2}\Upsilon }{\sqrt{n%
}}=O_{p}\left( 1\right) \text{ and }\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }UD_{\mu }^{-1}=O_{p}\left( \frac{n}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min
}\right) }\right) \text{,}
\end{equation*}%
so that $\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}XD_{\mu }^{-1}=O_{p}\left( n/\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) \right) $ and,
thus,%
\begin{eqnarray*}
\frac{\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}XD_{\mu }^{-1}}{n}D_{\mu }\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right)
&=&O_{p}\left( \frac{1}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\right) O_{p}\left(
1\right) \\
&=&O_{p}\left( \frac{1}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\right)
\end{eqnarray*}%
In addition, by part (a) of Lemma S2-2, we have in this case 
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }D_{\mu }\frac{%
D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }XD_{\mu }^{-1}}{n}D_{\mu
}\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) \\
&=&O_{p}\left( 1\right) O_{p}\left( \frac{1}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right)
^{2}}\right) O_{p}\left( 1\right) =O_{p}\left( \frac{1}{\left( \mu
_{n}^{\min }\right) ^{2}}\right) =o_{p}\left( 1\right) \text{,}
\end{eqnarray*}%
from which it follows that%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&\frac{\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) ^{\prime }M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) }{n} \\
&=&\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{n}+O_{p}\left( \frac{%
K_{1,n}}{n}\right) +O_{p}\left( \frac{1}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }%
\right) +O_{p}\left( \frac{1}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) ^{2}}\right) \\
&=&\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{n}+o_{p}\left( 1\right) 
\text{.}
\end{eqnarray*}%
Next, consider case (ii) where $\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) /\sqrt{K_{2,n}%
}=o\left( 1\right) $ but$\sqrt{K_{2,n}}/\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right)
^{2}\rightarrow 0$. Here, again by part (c) of Lemma OA-2 and expression (%
\ref{UMZ1Qe}); we have 
\begin{equation*}
\frac{\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}XD_{\mu }^{-1}}{n}=O_{p}\left( \frac{1}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }%
\right) =o_{p}\left( 1\right)
\end{equation*}%
so that%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&\frac{\left( y-X\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}XD_{\mu }^{-1}}{n}D_{\mu }\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) \\
&=&\frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\frac{\left(
y-X\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }XD_{\mu }^{-1}}{n}%
\frac{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) D_{\mu }\left( \widehat{\delta }%
_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}} \\
&=&O_{p}\left( \frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\right)
O_{p}\left( \frac{1}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) }\right) O_{p}\left(
1\right) =O_{p}\left( \frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right)
^{2}}\right) =o_{p}\left( 1\right) .
\end{eqnarray*}%
Furthermore, in this case,%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime }D_{\mu }\frac{%
D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }XD_{\mu }^{-1}}{n}D_{\mu
}\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) \\
&=&\frac{K_{2,n}}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) ^{2}}\frac{\left( \mu
_{n}^{\min }\right) \left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) ^{\prime
}D_{\mu }}{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}\frac{D_{\mu }^{-1}X^{\prime }M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }XD_{\mu }^{-1}}{n}\frac{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right)
D_{\mu }\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}-\delta _{0}\right) }{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}} \\
&=&O_{p}\left( \frac{K_{2,n}}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) ^{2}}\right)
O_{p}\left( 1\right) O_{p}\left( \frac{1}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) ^{2}%
}\right) O_{p}\left( 1\right) =O_{p}\left( \frac{K_{2,n}}{\left( \mu
_{n}^{\min }\right) ^{4}}\right) =o_{p}\left( 1\right)
\end{eqnarray*}%
from which it follows that in case (ii)%
\begin{eqnarray*}
\frac{\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) ^{\prime }M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) }{n} &=&\frac{%
\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{n}+O_{p}\left( \frac{K_{1,n}}{n}%
\right) +O_{p}\left( \frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right)
^{2}}\right) +O_{p}\left( \frac{K_{2,n}}{\left( \mu _{n}^{\min }\right) ^{4}}%
\right) \\
&=&\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{n}+o_{p}\left( 1\right)
\end{eqnarray*}%
Combining the results for cases (i) and (ii), we have%
\begin{equation*}
\frac{\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) ^{\prime }M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) }{n}=\frac{%
\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon }{n}+o_{p}\left( 1\right) \text{. }
\end{equation*}%
where $\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon /n=O_{p}\left( 1\right) $ and $%
\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon /n>0$ w.p.a.1. were both shown in the
proof of Lemma OA-5.

Finally, to show part (e), we apply the results of parts (c) and (d) above
to obtain%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&\widehat{\ell }\left( \widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) \\
&=&\frac{\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) ^{\prime }A\left( y-X%
\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) }{\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right)
^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) }
\\
&=&\frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{n}\frac{\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right)
^{\prime }A\left( y-X\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) /\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{\left( y-X%
\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) ^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }\left( y-X%
\widehat{\delta }_{n}\right) /n} \\
&=&\frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{n}\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }A\varepsilon /\sqrt{%
K_{2,n}}+o_{p}\left( 1\right) }{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon
/n+o_{p}\left( 1\right) } \\
&=&\frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{n}\left[ \frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }A\varepsilon /%
\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon /n}+o_{p}\left(
1\right) \right] \text{ \ }\left( \text{since }\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon }{n}>0\text{ w.p.a.1}\right) \\
&=&\frac{\varepsilon ^{\prime }A\varepsilon }{\varepsilon ^{\prime
}M^{Q}\varepsilon }+o_{p}\left( \frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{n}\right) =O_{p}\left( 
\frac{\sqrt{K_{2,n}}}{n}\right) \text{ }
\end{eqnarray*}%
given that $\varepsilon ^{\prime }A\varepsilon /\sqrt{K_{2,n}}=O_{p}\left(
1\right) $ and $\varepsilon ^{\prime }M^{Q}\varepsilon /n>0$ w.p.a.1. $%
\square $

\medskip

\noindent \noindent \textbf{Lemma OA-7: (Decoupling Inequality) }For natural
number $n\geq G$, let $\left\{ X_{i}\right\} _{i=1}^{n}$ be $n$ independent
random variables taking on values in a measurable space $\left( S,\mathfrak{S%
}\right) $, and let $\left\{ X_{i}^{\left( k\right) }\right\} _{i=1}^{n}$ $%
k=1,...,G$ be $G$ independent copies of this sequence. Let $B$ be a
separable Banach space and for each $\left( i_{1},..,i_{g_{\ast }}\right)
\in I_{n}^{g_{\ast }}$, where%
\begin{equation*}
I_{n}^{g_{\ast }}=\left\{ \left( i_{1},..,i_{g_{\ast }}\right) :i_{j}\in 
\mathbb{N}\text{, }1\leq i_{j}\leq n\text{, }i_{j}\neq i_{k}\text{ if }j\neq
k\right\} \text{,}
\end{equation*}%
let $h_{i_{1}...i_{G}}:S^{G}\longmapsto B$ be a measurable functions such
that $E\left( \left\Vert h_{i_{1}...i_{G}}\left(
X_{i_{1}},...,X_{i_{G}}\right) \right\Vert \right) <\infty $. Let $\Phi :%
\left[ 0,\infty \right) \longrightarrow \left[ 0,\infty \right) $ be a
convex nondecreasing function such that $E\Phi \left( \left\Vert
h_{i_{1}...i_{G}}\left( X_{i_{1}},...,X_{i_{G}}\right) \right\Vert \right)
<\infty $ for all $\left( i_{1},..,i_{G}\right) \in I_{n}^{G}$. Then, 
\begin{equation}
E\Phi \left( \left\Vert \dsum\limits_{I_{n}^{G}}h_{i_{1}...i_{G}}\left(
X_{i_{1}},...,X_{i_{G}}\right) \right\Vert \right) \leq E\Phi \left(
C_{G}\left\Vert \dsum\limits_{I_{n}^{G}}h_{i_{1}...i_{G}}\left(
X_{i_{1}},...,X_{i_{G}}\right) \right\Vert \right)  \label{decoupling ineq}
\end{equation}%
where $C_{G}=2^{G}\left[ G^{G}-1\right] \left[ \left( G-1\right) ^{\left(
G-1\right) }-1\right] \times \cdot \cdot \cdot \times 3$.

\medskip

\noindent Lemma OA-7 gives the inequality result stated in the first half of
Theorem 3.1.1 of de la Pe\~{n}a and Gin\'{e} (1999). Theorem 3.1.1 also
gives a reverse inequality under some additional symmetry conditions on the
kernel $h_{i_{1}...i_{G}}$ which we will not give here, since we will not be
using the reverse inequality any of the results stated below. Proof of a
more general decoupling inequality which contains the inequality given in
expression (\ref{decoupling ineq}) as a special case is provided in de la Pe%
\~{n}a (1992). See Theorem 2 of de la Pe\~{n}a (1992).

\medskip

\noindent \textbf{Lemma OA-8: }

Let $D\left( \varepsilon \circ \varepsilon \right) =diag\left( \varepsilon
_{\left( 1,1\right) }^{2},...,\varepsilon _{\left( n,T_{n}\right)
}^{2}\right) $. Under Assumptions 2, 5, and 6; the following statements hold.

\begin{enumerate}
\item[(a)] 
\begin{equation*}
\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D\left( \varepsilon \circ
\varepsilon \right) P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n}-\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime
}Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D_{\sigma ^{2}}P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n}%
=O_{p}\left( \sqrt{\frac{K_{2,n}}{n}}\right) \text{,}
\end{equation*}%
where $D_{\sigma ^{2}}=diag\left( E\left[ \varepsilon _{\left( 1,1\right)
}^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] ,....,E\left[ \varepsilon _{\left(
n,T_{n}\right) }^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \right) $.

\item[(b)] 
\begin{equation*}
\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }AD\left( \varepsilon \circ
\varepsilon \right) AZ_{2}\Upsilon }{n}-\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime
}Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }D_{\sigma ^{2}}M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n}=O_{p}\left( \sqrt{\frac{K_{2,n}}{n}}%
\right) =o_{p}\left( 1\right) \text{.}
\end{equation*}
\end{enumerate}

\bigskip

\noindent \textbf{Proof of Lemma OA-8:}

To show part (a), let $a,b\in \mathbb{R}^{d}$ such that $\left\Vert
a\right\Vert _{2}=\left\Vert b\right\Vert _{2}=1$, and note that we can write%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&\frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D\left(
\varepsilon \circ \varepsilon \right) P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon b}{n}-\frac{%
a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D_{\sigma
^{2}}P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon b}{n} \\
&=&\frac{1}{n}\dsum\limits_{\left( i,t\right)
=1}^{m_{n}}\dsum\limits_{\left( j,s\right) =1}^{m_{n}}\dsum\limits_{\left(
k,v\right) =1}^{m_{n}}P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( j,s\right) }^{\perp
}P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( k,v\right) }^{\perp }a^{\prime }\Upsilon
^{\prime }Z_{2,\left( j,s\right) }Z_{2,\left( k,v\right) }^{\prime }\Upsilon
b\left\{ \varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}-E\left[ \varepsilon _{\left(
i,t\right) }^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \right\}
\end{eqnarray*}%
Now, making use of the CS inequality as well as Assumptions 2(i), 3(iii) and
5; we obtain%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&E\left[ \left( \frac{1}{n}\dsum\limits_{\left( i,t\right)
=1}^{m_{n}}\dsum\limits_{\left( j,s\right) =1}^{m_{n}}\dsum\limits_{\left(
k,v\right) =1}^{m_{n}}P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( j,s\right) }^{\perp
}P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( k,v\right) }^{\perp }a^{\prime }\Upsilon
^{\prime }Z_{2,\left( j,s\right) }Z_{2,\left( k,v\right) }^{\prime }\Upsilon
b\left\{ \varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}-E\left[ \varepsilon _{\left(
i,t\right) }^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \right\} \right) ^{2}|\mathcal{F}%
_{n}^{Z}\right] \\
&=&\frac{1}{n^{2}}\dsum\limits_{\left( i,t\right)
=1}^{m_{n}}\dsum\limits_{\left( j,s\right) =1}^{m_{n}}\dsum\limits_{\left(
k,v\right) =1}^{m_{n}}\dsum\limits_{\left( \ell ,h\right)
=1}^{m_{n}}\dsum\limits_{\left( r,c\right) =1}^{m_{n}}P_{\left( i,t\right)
,\left( j,s\right) }^{\perp }P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( k,v\right)
}^{\perp }P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( \ell ,h\right) }^{\perp }P_{\left(
i,t\right) ,\left( r,c\right) }^{\perp } \\
&&\times \left( a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2,\left( j,s\right)
}\right) \left( a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2,\left( \ell ,h\right)
}\right) \left( Z_{2,\left( k,v\right) }^{\prime }\Upsilon b\right) \left(
Z_{2,\left( r,c\right) }^{\prime }\Upsilon b\right) E\left\{ \left(
\varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}-E\left[ \varepsilon _{\left(
i,t\right) }^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \right) ^{2}|\mathcal{F}%
_{n}^{Z}\right\} \\
&=&\frac{1}{n^{2}}\dsum\limits_{\left( i,t\right) =1}^{m_{n}}E\left\{ \left(
\varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}-E\left[ \varepsilon _{\left(
i,t\right) }^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \right) ^{2}|\mathcal{F}%
_{n}^{Z}\right\} \left( e_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime }P^{\perp
}Z_{2}\Upsilon a\right) ^{2}\left( e_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime }P^{\perp
}Z_{2}\Upsilon b\right) ^{2} \\
&\leq &\left( \max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}E\left[ \varepsilon
_{\left( i,t\right) }^{4}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \right) \frac{1}{n^{2}}%
\dsum\limits_{\left( i,t\right) =1}^{m_{n}}\left( a^{\prime }\Upsilon
^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }e_{\left( i,t\right) }e_{\left(
i,t\right) }^{\prime }P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon a\right) \left( b^{\prime
}\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }e_{\left( i,t\right) }e_{\left(
i,t\right) }^{\prime }P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon b\right) \\
&\leq &\left( \max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}E\left[ \varepsilon
_{\left( i,t\right) }^{4}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \right) \frac{1}{n}%
\left( a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp
}\dsum\limits_{\left( i,t\right) =1}^{m_{n}}e_{\left( i,t\right) }e_{\left(
i,t\right) }^{\prime }P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon a\right) e_{\left( i,t\right)
}^{\prime }P^{\perp }e_{\left( i,t\right) }\frac{b^{\prime }\Upsilon
^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }Z_{2}\Upsilon b}{n} \\
&\leq &\left( \max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}E\left[ \varepsilon
_{\left( i,t\right) }^{4}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \right) \left(
\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left(
i,t\right) }^{\perp }\right) \frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime
}Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon a}{n}\frac{b^{\prime }\Upsilon
^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }Z_{2}\Upsilon b}{n} \\
&=&O_{a.s.}\left( \frac{K_{2,n}}{n}\right) =o_{a.s.}\left( 1\right) .
\end{eqnarray*}%
Hence, there exists a constant $\overline{C}<\infty $ such that for all $n$
sufficiently large%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&E\left[ \frac{n}{K_{2,n}}\left( \frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime
}Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D\left( \varepsilon \circ \varepsilon \right)
P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon b}{n}-\frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime
}Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D_{\sigma ^{2}}P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon b}{n}%
\right) ^{2}\right] \\
&=&E_{Z}\left( \frac{n}{K_{2,n}}E\left[ \left( \frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon
^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D\left( \varepsilon \circ \varepsilon
\right) P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon b}{n}-\frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime
}Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D_{\sigma ^{2}}P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon b}{n}%
\right) ^{2}|\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \right) \leq \overline{C}\text{.}
\end{eqnarray*}%
It follows from the Markov's inequality that for any $\epsilon >0$,%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&\Pr \left( \sqrt{\frac{n}{K_{2,n}}}\left\vert \frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon
^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D\left( \varepsilon \circ \varepsilon
\right) P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon b}{n}-\frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime
}Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D_{\sigma ^{2}}P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon b}{n}%
\right\vert \geq \sqrt{\frac{\overline{C}}{\epsilon }}\right) \\
&=&\Pr \left( \frac{n}{K_{2,n}}\left( \frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime
}Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D\left( \varepsilon \circ \varepsilon \right)
P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon b}{n}-\frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime
}Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D_{\sigma ^{2}}P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon b}{n}%
\right) ^{2}\geq \frac{\overline{C}}{\epsilon }\right) \\
&\leq &\frac{\epsilon }{\overline{C}}E\left[ \frac{n}{K_{2,n}}\left( \frac{%
a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D\left( \varepsilon
\circ \varepsilon \right) P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon b}{n}-\frac{a^{\prime
}\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D_{\sigma ^{2}}P^{\perp
}Z_{2}\Upsilon b}{n}\right) ^{2}\right] \leq \epsilon
\end{eqnarray*}%
for all $n$ sufficiently large, which shows that%
\begin{equation*}
\frac{a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D\left(
\varepsilon \circ \varepsilon \right) P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon b}{n}-\frac{%
a^{\prime }\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D_{\sigma
^{2}}P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon b}{n}=O_{p}\left( \sqrt{\frac{K_{2,n}}{n}}%
\right) \text{.}
\end{equation*}%
Since the above result holds for all $a,b\in \mathbb{R}^{d}$ such that $%
\left\Vert a\right\Vert _{2}=\left\Vert b\right\Vert _{2}=1$, we further
deduce that%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D\left( \varepsilon
\circ \varepsilon \right) P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n}-\frac{\Upsilon
^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D_{\sigma ^{2}}P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n%
} \\
&=&\frac{1}{n}\dsum\limits_{\left( i,t\right)
=1}^{m_{n}}\dsum\limits_{\left( j,s\right) =1}^{m_{n}}\dsum\limits_{\left(
k,v\right) =1}^{m_{n}}P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( j,s\right) }^{\perp
}P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( k,v\right) }^{\perp }\gamma _{\left(
j,s\right) }\gamma _{\left( k,v\right) }^{\prime }\left\{ \varepsilon
_{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}-E\left[ \varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right) }^{2}|%
\mathcal{F}_{n}^{Z}\right] \right\} \\
&=&O_{p}\left( \sqrt{\frac{K_{2,n}}{n}}\right) .
\end{eqnarray*}

Next, consider part (b). Using the fact that $A=P^{\perp }-M^{\left(
Z,Q\right) }D_{\widehat{\vartheta }}M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }$ and that $%
M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }Z_{2}=0$ and applying the result of part (a) above, we
obtain 
\begin{eqnarray}
&&\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }AD\left( \varepsilon \circ
\varepsilon \right) AZ_{2}\Upsilon }{n}-\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime
}Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }D_{\sigma ^{2}}M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n}  \notag \\
&=&\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D\left( \varepsilon
\circ \varepsilon \right) P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n}-\frac{\Upsilon
^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }D_{\sigma ^{2}}M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n}  \notag \\
&&-\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }D_{\widehat{%
\vartheta }}M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }D\left( \varepsilon \circ \varepsilon
\right) P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n}-\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime
}P^{\perp }D\left( \varepsilon \circ \varepsilon \right) M^{\left(
Z,Q\right) }D_{\widehat{\vartheta }}M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n}
\notag \\
&&+\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }D_{\widehat{%
\vartheta }}M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }D\left( \varepsilon \circ \varepsilon
\right) M^{\left( Z,Q\right) }D_{\widehat{\vartheta }}M^{\left( Z,Q\right)
}Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n}  \notag \\
&=&\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D_{\sigma ^{2}}P^{\perp
}Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n}-\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }D_{\sigma ^{2}}M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n} 
\notag \\
&&+\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D\left( \varepsilon
\circ \varepsilon \right) P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n}-\frac{\Upsilon
^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D_{\sigma ^{2}}P^{\perp }Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n%
}  \notag \\
&=&\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D_{\sigma ^{2}}P^{\perp
}Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n}-\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }D_{\sigma ^{2}}M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n}%
+O_{p}\left( \sqrt{\frac{K_{2,n}}{n}}\right)  \label{Cov Mat1 approx 1}
\end{eqnarray}%
Next, note that%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{\perp }D_{\sigma ^{2}}P^{\perp
}Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n}-\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }D_{\sigma ^{2}}M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n}
\\
&=&\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}D_{\sigma ^{2}}M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n}-\frac{\Upsilon
^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }D_{\sigma ^{2}}M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n} \\
&&+\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }\left[ P^{\perp }-M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }\right] D_{\sigma ^{2}}M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n}+\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }D_{\sigma ^{2}}\left[ P^{\perp }-M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }%
\right] Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n} \\
&&+\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }\left[ P^{\perp }-M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }\right] D_{\sigma ^{2}}\left[ P^{\perp }-M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }\right] Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n} \\
&=&\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }\left[ P^{\perp }-M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }\right] D_{\sigma ^{2}}M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}Z_{2}\Upsilon }{n}+\frac{\Upsilon ^{\prime }Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left(
