\lambda _{\min }\left( \frac{Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}}{m_{n}}\right) \geq
C>0\text{ }a.s.\text{ for all }n\text{ sufficiently large.}
\end{equation*}

\item[(a2)] 
\begin{equation*}
\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}\left( \frac{1}{K_{1,n}}%
\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{1,n}}Z_{1,\left( i,t\right) ,k}^{2}\right)
=O_{a.s.}\left( 1\right)
\end{equation*}
\end{enumerate}

Under conditions (a1) and (a2), 
\begin{equation*}
\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left(
i,t\right) }^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}=O_{a.s.}\left( \frac{K_{1,n}}{n}\right) \text{,%
}
\end{equation*}%
where $P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( i,t\right) }^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}$ is the $%
\left( \left( i,t\right) ,\left( i,t\right) \right) ^{th}$ of the projection
matrix $P^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}$.

\item[(b)] Assume the following conditions hold:

\begin{enumerate}
\item[(b1)] There exists a positive constant $C$ such that%
\begin{equation*}
\lambda _{\min }\left( \frac{Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }Z_{2}}{%
m_{n}}\right) \geq C>0\text{ }a.s.\text{ for all }n\text{ sufficiently large.%
}
\end{equation*}

\item[(b2)] 
\begin{equation*}
\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}\left( \frac{1}{K_{2,n}}%
\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{2,n}}Z_{2,\left( i,s\right) ,k}^{2}\right)
=O_{a.s.}\left( 1\right) \text{.}
\end{equation*}

\item[(b3)] 
\begin{equation*}
\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}\left( \frac{1}{K_{2,n}}%
\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{2,n}}\widetilde{Z}_{2,\left( i,s\right)
,k}^{2}\right) =O_{a.s.}\left( 1\right) \text{.}
\end{equation*}
\end{enumerate}

Under conditions (b1)-(b3, 
\begin{equation*}
\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left(
i,t\right) }^{\perp }=O_{a.s.}\left( \frac{K_{2,n}}{n}\right) \text{,}
\end{equation*}%
where $P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left( i,t\right) }^{\perp }$ is the $\left(
\left( i,t\right) ,\left( i,t\right) \right) ^{th}$ of the projection matrix

$P^{\perp }=M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }Z_{2}\left( Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }Z_{2}\right) ^{-1}Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }$.
\end{enumerate}

\noindent \textbf{Proof of Lemma OA-20:}

To show part (a), . Note that%
\begin{eqnarray*}
0 &\leq &\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}P_{\left( i,t\right)
,\left( i,t\right) }^{Z_{1}^{\perp }} \\
&=&\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}e_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime
}M^{Q}Z_{1}\left( Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}\right) ^{-1}Z_{1}^{\prime
}M^{Q}e_{\left( i,t\right) } \\
&=&\frac{1}{m_{n}}\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}e_{\left(
i,t\right) }^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}\left( \frac{Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}}{m_{n}%
}\right) ^{-1}Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}e_{\left( i,t\right) } \\
&\leq &\frac{1}{\lambda _{\min }\left( Z_{1}^{\prime
}M^{Q}Z_{1}/m_{n}\right) }\frac{1}{m_{n}}\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq
m_{n}}e_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}Z_{1}^{\prime
}M^{Q}e_{\left( i,t\right) } \\
&\leq &\frac{1}{C}\frac{1}{m_{n}}\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq
m_{n}}\left\{ \dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{1,n}}e_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime
}M^{Q}Z_{1,\cdot ,k}Z_{1,\cdot ,k}^{\prime }M^{Q}e_{\left( i,t\right)
}\right\} \\
&=&\frac{1}{C}\frac{1}{m_{n}}\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq
m_{n}}\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{1,n}}\left( e_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime
}M^{Q}Z_{1,\cdot ,k}\right) ^{2} \\
&=&\frac{1}{C}\frac{1}{m_{n}}\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq
m_{n}}\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{1,n}}\left( Z_{1,\left( i,t\right)
,k}-T_{i}^{-1}\dsum\nolimits_{s=1}^{T_{i}}Z_{1,\left( i,s\right) ,k}\right)
^{2} \\
&\leq &\frac{2}{C}\frac{1}{m_{n}}\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}%
\left[ \dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{1,n}}Z_{1,\left( i,t\right)
,k}^{2}+\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{1,n}}\left( \frac{1}{T_{i}}%
\dsum\limits_{s=1}^{T_{i}}Z_{1,\left( i,s\right) ,k}\right) ^{2}\right] \\
&&\left( \text{by applying the inequality }\left\vert
\dsum\limits_{i=1}^{m}a_{i}\right\vert ^{r}\leq
m^{r-1}\dsum\limits_{i=1}^{m}\left\vert a_{i}\right\vert ^{r}\text{ for }%
r\geq 1\right) \\
&\leq &\frac{2}{C}\frac{1}{m_{n}}\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}%
\left[ \dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{1,n}}Z_{1,\left( i,t\right)
,k}^{2}+\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{1,n}}\frac{1}{T_{i}}\dsum%
\limits_{s=1}^{T_{i}}Z_{1,\left( i,s\right) ,k}^{2}\right] \text{ }\left( 
\text{by Jensen's inequality}\right)
\end{eqnarray*}%
Hence, by multiplying and dividing the majorant side of the above expression
by $K_{1,n}$ and making use of the assumption that 
\begin{equation*}
\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}\left( \frac{1}{K_{1,n}}%
\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{1,n}}Z_{1,\left( i,t\right) ,k}^{2}\right)
=O_{a.s.}\left( 1\right) \text{;}
\end{equation*}%
we obtain%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left(
i,t\right) }^{Z_{1}^{\perp }} \\
&\leq &\frac{2}{C}\frac{K_{1,n}}{m_{n}}\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq
m_{n}}\left[ \frac{1}{K_{1,n}}\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{1,n}}Z_{1,\left(
i,t\right) ,k}^{2}+\frac{1}{T_{i}}\dsum\limits_{s=1}^{T_{i}}\left( \frac{1}{%
K_{1,n}}\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{1,n}}Z_{1,\left( i,s\right) ,k}^{2}\right) %
\right] \\
&\leq &\frac{2}{C}\frac{K_{1,n}}{m_{n}}\left[ \max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right)
\leq m_{n}}\left( \frac{1}{K_{1,n}}\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{1,n}}Z_{1,\left(
i,t\right) ,k}^{2}\right) +\frac{1}{T_{i}}\dsum\limits_{s=1}^{T_{i}}\max_{1%
\leq \left( i,s\right) \leq m_{n}}\left( \frac{1}{K_{1,n}}%
\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{1,n}}Z_{1,\left( i,s\right) ,k}^{2}\right) \right] \\
&=&O_{a.s.}\left( \frac{K_{1,n}}{m_{n}}\right) =O_{a.s.}\left( \frac{K_{1,n}%
}{n}\right)
\end{eqnarray*}%
given that $m_{n}\sim n$.

To show part (b), note that%
\begin{eqnarray*}
0 &\leq &\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}P_{\left( i,t\right)
,\left( i,t\right) }^{\perp } \\
&=&\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}e_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime
}M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }Z_{2}\left( Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }Z_{2}\right) ^{-1}Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}e_{\left( i,t\right) } \\
&=&\frac{1}{m_{n}}\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}e_{\left(
i,t\right) }^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }Z_{2}\left( \frac{%
Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }Z_{2}}{m_{n}}\right)
^{-1}Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }e_{\left( i,t\right) } \\
&\leq &\frac{1}{\lambda _{\min }\left( Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }Z_{2}/m_{n}\right) }\frac{1}{m_{n}}\max_{1\leq \left(
i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}e_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime }M^{\left(
Z_{1},Q\right) }Z_{2}Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }e_{\left(
i,t\right) } \\
&\leq &\frac{1}{C}\frac{1}{m_{n}}\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq
m_{n}}e_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}Z_{2}Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }e_{\left( i,t\right) }
\end{eqnarray*}%
Next, observe that%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&e_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right)
}Z_{2}Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{\left( Z_{1},Q\right) }e_{\left( i,t\right) } \\
&=&e_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime }\left[ M^{Q}-P^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}\right]
Z_{2}Z_{2}^{\prime }\left[ M^{Q}-P^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}\right] e_{\left(
i,t\right) } \\
&=&e_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{2}Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{Q}e_{\left(
i,t\right) }-2e_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime }P^{Z_{1}^{\perp
}}Z_{2}Z_{2}^{\prime }M^{Q}e_{\left( i,t\right) }+e_{\left( i,t\right)
}^{\prime }P^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}Z_{2}Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}e_{\left(
i,t\right) } \\
&\leq &2e_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{2}Z_{2}^{\prime
}M^{Q}e_{\left( i,t\right) }+2e_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime
}P^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}Z_{2}Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}e_{\left(
i,t\right) } \\
&&\left( \text{by applying the inequality }\left\vert
\dsum\limits_{i=1}^{m}a_{i}\right\vert ^{r}\leq
m^{r-1}\dsum\limits_{i=1}^{m}\left\vert a_{i}\right\vert ^{r}\text{ for }%
r\geq 1\right)
\end{eqnarray*}%
where $P^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}=M^{Q}Z_{1}\left( Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{1}\right)
^{-1}Z_{1}^{\prime }M^{Q}$. It follows that we can write 
\begin{eqnarray*}
0 &\leq &\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}P_{\left( i,t\right)
,\left( i,t\right) }^{\perp } \\
&\leq &\frac{2}{C}\frac{1}{m_{n}}\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq
m_{n}}\left\{ e_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{2}Z_{2}^{\prime
}M^{Q}e_{\left( i,t\right) }+e_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime }P^{Z_{1}^{\perp
}}Z_{2}Z_{2}^{\prime }P^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}e_{\left( i,t\right) }\right\} \\
&\leq &\frac{2}{C}\frac{1}{m_{n}}\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq
m_{n}}\left\{ \dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{2,n}}e_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime
}M^{Q}Z_{2,\cdot ,k}Z_{2,\cdot ,k}^{\prime }M^{Q}e_{\left( i,t\right)
}+\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{2,n}}e_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime
}P^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}Z_{2,\cdot ,k}Z_{2,\cdot ,k}^{\prime }P^{Z_{1}^{\perp
}}e_{\left( i,t\right) }\right\} \\
&=&\frac{1}{C}\frac{1}{m_{n}}\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq
m_{n}}\left\{ \dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{2,n}}\left( e_{\left( i,t\right)
}^{\prime }M^{Q}Z_{2,\cdot ,k}\right)
^{2}+\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{2,n}}\left( e_{\left( i,t\right) }^{\prime
}P^{Z_{1}^{\perp }}Z_{2,\cdot ,k}\right) ^{2}\right\} \\
&=&\frac{1}{C}\frac{1}{m_{n}}\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq
m_{n}}\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{2,n}}\left( Z_{2,\left( i,t\right)
,k}-T_{i}^{-1}\dsum\nolimits_{s=1}^{T_{i}}Z_{2,\left( i,s\right) ,k}\right)
^{2}+\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{2,n}}\widetilde{Z}_{2,\left( i,t\right) ,k}^{2}
\\
&\leq &\frac{2}{C}\frac{1}{m_{n}}\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}%
\left[ \dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{1,n}}Z_{2,\left( i,t\right)
,k}^{2}+\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{2,n}}\left( \frac{1}{T_{i}}%
\dsum\limits_{s=1}^{T_{i}}Z_{2,\left( i,s\right) ,k}\right)
^{2}+\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{2,n}}\widetilde{Z}_{2,\left( i,t\right) ,k}^{2}%
\right] \\
&&\left( \text{by applyng the inequality }\left\vert
\dsum\limits_{i=1}^{m}a_{i}\right\vert ^{r}\leq
m^{r-1}\dsum\limits_{i=1}^{m}\left\vert a_{i}\right\vert ^{r}\text{ for }%
r\geq 1\right) \\
&\leq &\frac{2}{C}\frac{1}{m_{n}}\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}%
\left[ \dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{1,n}}Z_{1,\left( i,t\right)
,k}^{2}+\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{1,n}}\frac{1}{T_{i}}\dsum%
\limits_{s=1}^{T_{i}}Z_{1,\left( i,s\right)
,k}^{2}+\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{2,n}}\widetilde{Z}_{2,\left( i,t\right)
,k}^{2}\right] \text{ }\left( \text{by Jensen's inequality}\right)
\end{eqnarray*}%
Hence, by multiplying and dividing the majorant side of the above expression
by $K_{2,n}$ and making use of the assumptions that 
\begin{equation*}
\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}\left( \frac{1}{K_{2,n}}%
\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{2,n}}Z_{2,\left( i,t\right) ,k}^{2}\right)
=O_{a.s.}\left( 1\right) \text{ and }\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq
m_{n}}\left( \frac{1}{K_{2,n}}\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{2,n}}\widetilde{Z}%
_{2,\left( i,t\right) ,k}^{2}\right) =O_{a.s.}\left( 1\right) \text{;}
\end{equation*}%
we obtain%
\begin{eqnarray*}
&&\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq m_{n}}P_{\left( i,t\right) ,\left(
i,t\right) }^{Z_{1}^{\perp }} \\
&\leq &\frac{2}{C}\frac{K_{2,n}}{m_{n}}\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right) \leq
m_{n}}\left[ \frac{1}{K_{2,n}}\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{2,n}}Z_{2,\left(
i,t\right) ,k}^{2}+\frac{1}{T_{i}}\dsum\limits_{s=1}^{T_{i}}\left( \frac{1}{%
K_{2,n}}\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{2,n}}Z_{2,\left( i,s\right) ,k}^{2}\right) +%
\frac{1}{K_{2,n}}\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{2,n}}\widetilde{Z}_{2,\left(
i,t\right) ,k}^{2}\right] \\
&\leq &\frac{2}{C}\frac{K_{2,n}}{m_{n}}\left[ \max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right)
\leq m_{n}}\left( \frac{1}{K_{2,n}}\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{2,n}}Z_{2,\left(
i,t\right) ,k}^{2}\right) +\frac{1}{T_{i}}\dsum\limits_{s=1}^{T_{i}}\max_{1%
\leq \left( i,s\right) \leq m_{n}}\left( \frac{1}{K_{1,n}}%
\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{2,n}}Z_{2,\left( i,s\right) ,k}^{2}\right) \right. \\
&&\text{ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ }\left. +\max_{1\leq \left( i,t\right)
\leq m_{n}}\left( \frac{1}{K_{2,n}}\dsum\limits_{k=1}^{K_{2,n}}\widetilde{Z}%
_{2,\left( i,t\right) ,k}^{2}\right) \right] \\
&=&O_{a.s.}\left( \frac{K_{2,n}}{m_{n}}\right) =O_{a.s.}\left( \frac{K_{2,n}%
}{n}\right)
\end{eqnarray*}%
given that $m_{n}\sim n$. $\square $

\medskip

\section{\noindent Section 4: Additional Monte Carlo Results}

This section reports some additional Monte Carlo results which complement
those presented in the main paper. Whereas the class of DGPs which generated
the Monte Carlo results in the main paper concerns weakly identified
situations where the instruments are all relevant but have uniformly small
coefficients; the Monte Carlo design presented here considers a more
heterogeneous case where there is one weak but relevant instrument while all
other instruments used in estimation are completely irrelevant. More
precisely, the Monte Carlo results reported here are based on the following
data generating process:

\noindent \textbf{DGP*:}%
\begin{eqnarray*}
y_{\left( i,t\right) } &=&\underset{1\times 1}{\delta }\underset{1\times 1}{%
x_{\left( i,t\right) }}+\underset{1\times 10}{\varphi ^{\prime }}\underset{%
10\times 1}{Z_{1,\left( i,t\right) }}+\alpha _{i}+\varepsilon _{\left(
i,t\right) }\text{,} \\
x_{\left( i,t\right) } &=&\underset{1\times 10}{\Phi ^{\prime }}\underset{%
10\times 1}{Z_{1,\left( i,t\right) }}+\underset{1\times 1}{\pi }\underset{%
1\times 1}{z_{21,\left( i,t\right) }}+\xi _{i}+u_{\left( i,t\right) }\text{.}
\end{eqnarray*}%
Here, we specify $\varphi =\iota _{10}$ and $\Phi =\iota _{10}$, with $\iota
_{10}$ being a $10\times 1$ vector of ones; and we choose the scalar
parameter $\pi $ so that the concentration parameter $\mu ^{2}=25,$ $35,$ $%
45,$ and $55$. The $\left( i,t\right) ^{th}$ observation of the vector of
instruments used in estimation is taken to be the $K_{2}\times 1$ vector $%
Z_{2,\left( i,t\right) }=\left( 
\begin{array}{cccc}
z_{21,\left( i,t\right) } & z_{22,\left( i,t\right) } & \cdots & 
z_{2K_{2},\left( i,t\right) }%
\end{array}%
\right) ^{\prime }$, where $\left\{ Z_{2,\left( i,t\right) }\right\}
_{\left( i,t\right) =1}^{600}\equiv i.i.d.N\left( 0,I_{K_{2}}\right) $; and
we consider two choices of $K_{2}$: $K_{2}=10,30$. On the other hand, the $%
\left( i,t\right) ^{th}$ observation of the vector of included exogenous
regressors, or covariates, is specified to be

\noindent\ $Z_{1,\left( i,t\right) }=\left( 
\begin{array}{ccccccc}
z_{1,\left( i,t\right) } & z_{1,\left( i,t\right) }^{2} & z_{1,\left(
i,t\right) }^{3} & z_{1,\left( i,t\right) }^{4} & z_{1,\left( i,t\right)
}D_{\left( i,t\right) ,1} & \cdots & z_{1,\left( i,t\right) }D_{\left(
i,t\right) ,6}%
\end{array}%
\right) ^{\prime }$, where $\left\{ z_{1,\left( i,t\right) }\right\}
_{\left( i,t\right) =1}^{600}\equiv i.i.d.N\left( 0,1\right) $ and $%
D_{\left( i,t\right) ,k}\in \left\{ 0,1\right\} $ for $k\in \left\{
1,2,..,6\right\} $ is a binary variable such that $\Pr \left( D_{\left(
i,t\right) ,k}=1\right) =1/2,$ with $\left\{ D_{\left( i,t\right)
,k}\right\} $ taken to be independent across both $\left( i,t\right) $ and $%
k $. Moreover, in our experiments, we set $n=200$ and $T_{i}=3,$ for each $%
i\in \left\{ 1,2,...,200\right\} $, so that $m_{n}=600$. We also take $%
\left\{ u_{\left( i,t\right) }\right\} _{\left( i,t\right) =1}^{600}\equiv
i.i.d.N\left( 0,1\right) $, $\left\{ \alpha _{i}\right\}
_{i=1}^{200}i.i.d.N\left( 0,1\right) $, and $\left\{ \xi _{i}\right\}
_{i=1}^{200}i.i.d.N\left( 0,1\right) $; and $z_{1,\left( i,t\right) }$, $%
D_{\left( i,t\right) ,k}$, $Z_{2,\left( i,t\right) }$, $u_{\left( i,t\right)
}$, $\alpha _{i}$ and $\xi _{i}$ are all specified to be independent of each
other. We allow the structural disturbance, $\varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right)
},$ to exhibit conditional heteroskedasticity in a manner similar to the
design given in Hausman et al (2012) and in our main paper. In particular,
we let%
\begin{equation}
\varepsilon _{\left( i,t\right) }=\rho u_{\left( i,t\right) }+\sqrt{\frac{%
1-\rho ^{2}}{\phi ^{2}+\left( 0.86\right) ^{2}}}\left( \phi v_{1,\left(
i,t\right) }+0.86v_{2,\left( i,t\right) }\right) ,  \label{epsilon}
\end{equation}%
where $v_{1,\left( i,t\right) }|Z_{1,\left( i,t\right) },z_{21,\left(
i,t\right) }\sim N\left( 0,\kappa \left[ 1+\left( \iota _{10}^{\prime
}Z_{1,\left( i,t\right) }+z_{21,\left( i,t\right) }\right) ^{2}\right]
\right) $ and $v_{2,\left( i,t\right) }\sim N\left( 0,1\right) $. Both of
these distributions are specified to be independent across the index $\left(
i,t\right) $, and $\kappa $ is a normalization constant chosen so that the
unconditional variance, $Var\left( v_{1,\left( i,t\right) }\right) $, is
equal to 1. For all experiments reported below, we set $\rho =0.3$ and we
choose the parameter $\phi $, so that the R-squared for the regression of $%
\varepsilon ^{2}$ on the instruments and the included exogenous variables
take the values $0$, $0.1$, and $0.2$.

\noindent \qquad The results of our Monte Carlo study based on the above
data generating process are reported in Tables A1- A6 below.

& \multicolumn{1}{|c|}{0} & \multicolumn{1}{|c|}{0.1701} &

\multicolumn{1}{|c|}{0.0553} & \multicolumn{1}{|c|}{0.0570} \\ \cline{2-9}
& \multicolumn{1}{|c|}{0.2} & \multicolumn{1}{|c|}{0.1855} & 
\multicolumn{1}{|c|}{0.0933} & \multicolumn{1}{|c|}{0.0879} &

{\small Results based on 10,000 simulations}

Qualitatively, the results presented in Tables A1-A6 mirror the results
given in Tables 1-6 of the main paper. In particular, note that, in terms of
median bias, the performance of FEJIV, FELIM, and FEFUL are uniformly
better, across all our experiments, when compared to 2SLS, IJIVE1, IJIVE2,
and UJIVE; but our experiments do show 2SLS, IJIVE1, and IJIVE2 to be less
dispersed than the three estimators proposed in this paper. Again, perhaps
the most notable difference in performance is that t-statistics based on
FELIM\ and FEFUL have much less size distortion than t-statistics
constructed from any of the other five estimators. Overall, the results here
seem to indicate that allowing for some instruments to be completely
irrelevant does not seem to yield results that are substantially different
from the case where all instruments are taken to be relevant but weak, as
long as the magnitude of the concentration parameter is kept the same in
both cases.

York: John Wiley \& Sons.

Wahrscheinlichkeitstheorie}. New York: Springer-Verlag.

\bibitem{} Hall, P. and C. Heyde (1980). \textit{Martingale Limit Theory and
Its Applications. }New York: Academic Press.

\bibitem{} Horn, R.A. and C. R. Johnson (1985). \textit{Matrix Analysis}.
Cambridge: Cambridge University Press.
\end{thebibliography}
